  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a506260a-886a-4798-adc1-57f9a3974b81'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="review_2237980481" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2237980481" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52930632-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554853474p2/52930632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2237980481?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/52930632-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062885753" href="/book/show/40535692-a-crystal-of-time">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=i-will-read-anything-by-this-author">i-will-read-anything-by-this-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=hyped-af-to-read">hyped-af-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=illustrated">illustrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=rollercoaster-of-feelings">rollercoaster-of-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=laughed-out-loud">laughed-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=nearly-perfect">nearly-perfect</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2237980481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18387191623802518478"><blockquote>
  <i>I can be the One True King, the immortal Lion, cutting the head off every Snake.</i>
</blockquote><b>4.98 stars</b><p><b><u>CAN YOU HEAR ME SCREAMING???????</u></b> Holy friggin shit I am BUZZIN' right now with the adrenaline because holy hell there were so many plot twists in Part 2 alone. Soman knows how to write a plot, that's for sure.</p><p>After <u>THAT CLIFFHANGER</u> in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31212082.Quests_for_Glory__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil_The_Camelot_Years___1_' title='Quests for Glory (The School for Good and Evil The Camelot Years, #1) by Soman Chainani' rel='nofollow noopener'>Quests for Glory</a>, we open with Agatha running for her life, Sophie trapped at swordpoint and essentially all the protagonists in jail or otherwise dire straits. <b>Sophie, Ho</b></p></span>
  <span id="freeText18387191623802518478" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I can be the One True King, the immortal Lion, cutting the head off every Snake.</i>
</blockquote><b>4.98 stars</b><p><b><u>CAN YOU HEAR ME SCREAMING???????</u></b> Holy friggin shit I am BUZZIN' right now with the adrenaline because holy hell there were so many plot twists in Part 2 alone. Soman knows how to write a plot, that's for sure.</p><p>After <u>THAT CLIFFHANGER</u> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31212082.Quests_for_Glory__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil_The_Camelot_Years___1_" title="Quests for Glory (The School for Good and Evil The Camelot Years, #1) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">Quests for Glory</a>, we open with Agatha running for her life, Sophie trapped at swordpoint and essentially all the protagonists in jail or otherwise dire straits. <b>Sophie, Hort and Tedros had my favourite POVs</b> in this instalment, and how they react to the new obstacles that get thrown in their very messy paths illustrate just how much they're growing and self-reflecting - and I loved that. Especially Teddy (about goddamn time!). Also shoutout to Beatrix too! <b>All the women in this book were pretty kickass tbh, even the Evil ones.</b> If this isn't the most Sophie gif ever:</p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552170995ra/27182035.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><p>I did find that <b>Part 1 wasn't as engrossing as I'd expected</b>, what with the incredibly high stakes, but there were enough <b>shocking reveals and unexpected turns</b> that I had to start noting down my theories - it was just so twisty! <b>Part 2 is where it <i>really</i> kicks off.</b> I was literally <i>fanning myself</i> because I had so much adrenaline from reading. It wasn't just the plot twists, chilling foreshadowing or ridiculously intense scene immediately preceding Part 2, but the <b>thought-provoking questions that are so classic to SGE.</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42080479.The_School_for_Good_and_Evil__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___1_" title="The School for Good and Evil (The School for Good and Evil, #1) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">The School for Good and Evil</a> was a brilliant take on subversive fairytale tropes, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18172465.A_World_Without_Princes__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___2_" title="A World Without Princes (The School for Good and Evil, #2) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">A World Without Princes</a> spotlighted issues of extreme 'feminism' (where it's not even recognisably feminism anymore) and toxic masculinity, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18004320.The_Last_Ever_After__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___3_" title="The Last Ever After (The School for Good and Evil, #3) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Ever After</a> had a central question of what decides a 'happy' ending, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31212082.Quests_for_Glory__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil_The_Camelot_Years___1_" title="Quests for Glory (The School for Good and Evil The Camelot Years, #1) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">Quests for Glory</a> pondered on the line between Truth and Lies, Good and Evil - if one even exists. <b><i>A Crystal of Time</i>, through the characterisation of Rhian and POVs of Sophie (both <i>wonderfully</i> complex characters, by the way), asks us if the means justify the end.</b> If The End is the eradication of <i>all</i> Evil, not just that of one fairytale...what would you give up to make it happen?</p><blockquote>
  <i>I spent my life in the shadows, where Good and Evil are never so simple. Every day in my world requires sacrifices. Sacrifices that can be awful and ugly. But I want a better future for people like me... a King of the <u>People</u> must rise. Any Evil I've done, any lie I've told, it's to make that future possible.</i>
</blockquote>I personally think that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rhian is the 100% Good twin, and Japeth is the 100% Evil twin - unfortunately Rhian isn't Japeth's true love the way Agatha is Sophie's. RIP bb, I actually mourned wtf <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <b>This book accompanied its plot twists with a hefty dose of SGE-brand hilarity</b>, though for some reason I didn't cry when I expected I would. I also felt like <b>some reveals were a tad info-dumpy</b>, for example about the rings. Others like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Reaper's backstory <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were excusable because they were dramatic monologues and carried the story along. <b>OTHER REVEALS HIT ME IN THE FACE LIKE A TON OF BRICKS</b>...or should I say ton of butterflies???<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552171085ra/27182036.gif" width="380" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><p><b>All in all, I really enjoyed this!!</b> Absolutely hyped for the next book (which is going to be the final one *sob*).</p><u>Some predictions/questions for Book 6 (marked spoilers):</u><br>- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Japeth and Sophie's wedding <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> will <i>not</i> happen as scheduled, Willam and Bogden have never been wrong before (despite it all happening in such a roundabout fashion)<br>- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Japeth was Rhian's <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Snake instead of Tedros. I don't think Tedros was even part of that story. Sophie/Kei was kind of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Eagle in Rhian's fairytale. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>- Why does <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Evelyn's dress <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> like Sophie?!??<br>- WHAT DID THE LADY OF THE LAKE SENSE WHEN SHE <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[kissed Japeth <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> like come onnnnnn way to leave us on a cliffhanger!!<br>- Sophie better be <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[safe, escape scimmy mind control and survive all six books otherwise JAPETH <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> CAN CATCH THESE HANDS<br>----------------------------------------------------<br><b>THE BOOK IS IN MY HAAAAAANDS - three days early!!!</b> <u>Stay away from my updates though I won't post spoilers/will clearly mark if I do!</u><p>As far as I know, Book 5 is set for a 2018 release. It is now 2018.</p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456475747ra/18238088.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><p><b>Update:</b> As of March 23 2018 it is now set for a March 2019 release - pleeease be worth it &lt;3 </p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521892178ra/25266904.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18387191623802518478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2153315204" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2153315204" />
    <a title="Elis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63448796-elis"><img alt="Elis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515672104p2/63448796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2153315204?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_2122664870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122664870" />
    <a title="Nikita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23919282-nikita"><img alt="Nikita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496262143p2/23919282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2122664870?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikita" href="/user/show/23919282-nikita">Nikita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23919282-nikita?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23919282-nikita?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23919282-nikita?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2122664870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4561570754717090007">Updated March 21, 2019:<br/>A Crystal of Time is exciting, emotional, gripping, shocking and amazing. A false king has taken over Camelot’s throne, sentencing its true king, Tedros to death while Agatha barely escaping capture. Sophie is trapped to become Rhian’s queen and with her wedding fast approaching, she is forced to play a dangerous game to protect her friends. With King Rhian’s dark plans for Camelot taking shape, Agatha and the students of the School for Good and Evil must find a way to res</span>
  <span id="freeText4561570754717090007" style="display:none">Updated March 21, 2019:<br>A Crystal of Time is exciting, emotional, gripping, shocking and amazing. A false king has taken over Camelot’s throne, sentencing its true king, Tedros to death while Agatha barely escaping capture. Sophie is trapped to become Rhian’s queen and with her wedding fast approaching, she is forced to play a dangerous game to protect her friends. With King Rhian’s dark plans for Camelot taking shape, Agatha and the students of the School for Good and Evil must find a way to restore Tedros to the throne before their stories and the future of the Endless Woods are rewritten forever. A Crystal of Time is filled with magic, adventure, shock, danger, mystery, discovery, emotion, and twists.<br><br>After Rhian takes over Camelot, sentencing Tedros to death and her friends captured, Agatha barely escapes and now flees for her life. After learning a shocking discovery, Agatha with no allies, no friends and hunted by Rhian, Agatha finds hope at the School for Good &amp; Evil. There Agatha must train the students to become her army only to find mystery and discovery about Rhian’s plans for the Woods as the Storian’s power is threaten. With the help of friends Agatha was able to rescue her friends and with the help of a very unlikely ally form a plan in hopes of stopping Rhian’s evil. As the teachers, students, coven and friends go on their quests, Agatha, Tedros and Sophie go into Dovey’s crystal ball to search for answers to how Rhian is king. As Rhian’s hold over the Woods gets stronger, Agatha and friends make one discovery after another into Rhian and the Snake’s past as they try to find a way to stop his plans and take back the Woods for good.<br><br>Tedros along with his friends, Professor Dovey, Merlin and his mother are being held prisoner by Rhian who he thought he trusted but has taken his crown and worse has been sentenced Tedros to death. After being rescued, Tedros and friends learns of Rhian’s plans that threaten the Storian and the Woods and while his friends, the school teachers, and other students have quests of their own to stop Rhian’s evil with the help of a very unlikely ally, he, Agatha and Sophie go on a quest of their own to discover one shock after another with the aid of Dovey’s crystal ball. As Rhian’s hold over the Woods gets stronger, Tedros comes to grip over one discovery after another into Rhian and the Snake’s past as he, Agatha and try friends try to take back the throne and stop evil.<br><br>Sophie forced to become Rhian’s queen in order to protect her friends and to discover the truth behind Rhian and the Snake revealed to be alive and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ his twin brother, Japeth  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> plan for Camelot and the Woods, Sophie plays a dangerous game. To keep her friends alive, Sophie is forced to write stories using Rhian’s pen to tell lies to further claim that Rhian is king and Tedros a fake. Sophie continues to learn more about Rhian’s plan for the Woods, leaving her shocked and fearful for her friends as his lies continue to spread throughout the Woods. After escaping Camelot, rejoining her friends, Sophie aides them to stop Rhian evil by helping Agatha and Tedros discover more about Rhian’s past. However, Sophie’s attempt to stop Rhian and the Snake only unleashes a more deadlier evil upon those she cares for.<br><br>Held prisoner in Camelot’s dungeon, the trio, Nicola, Hort, Professor Dovey, and other members of the quest team are being held prisoner by Rhian. As they try to find a way to escape, they also try to learn more about Rhian’s history and motives for Camelot and the Endless Woods before it is too late. After being rescued, the quest team learn of Rhian’s evil and his plan for the Woods with help from the school’s teachers, other students and a very unlikely ally break into teams to learn more about Rhian’s past, protect the school, rescue Merlin and ensure that other kingdoms don’t turn against them while Agatha, Sophie and Tedros go on a quest of their own.<br><br>Everyone is struggling with Rhian as King of Camelot and it not only breaks my heart to see them like this but it angers me. I hated to see what was happening and the pain he was causing to my beloved characters. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ One of Anadil’s rats is killed. Professor Dovey dies. Reaper can talk and is a king?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I hate Rhian and the Snake. Both are just twisted, manipulative and more evil than Rafel if that is even possible. <br><br>Overall, A Crystal of Time was emotional and amazing. I love this series so much. Soman is amazing. To make me feel so engulfed in this story that I can have such emotion is incredible. The characters remain great, the setting and story is incredible and the pace never gets trying. Be warned that there are deaths in this tale and shock and twist after shock and twist. I need the next book, I have questions that need answers and OMG the wait is already killing me. This is one of my top favorite fairy tale retelling series of all. <br><br>Updated May 25, 2018:<br>OMG! It has a cover!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1527267405i/25596567._SY540_.jpg" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So beautiful!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433961954ra/15162469.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I want it! I want it! I want it!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403813583ra/10148557.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2147274256" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2147274256" />
    <a title="Ramona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52524382-ramona"><img alt="Ramona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604282330p2/52524382.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2147274256?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ramona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ramona" href="/user/show/52524382-ramona">Ramona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2147274256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18030338878489155994">Well done, Chainani, well done.<br/><br/>A <i>significantly</i> more delightful book than the previous, and much less frustrating; my poor, tired heart is very thankful. It was more-so a rollercoaster that slowed down, picked up, slowed down, picked up, and kept switching that around until the end where it’s like forty loops in one go. <i>And I loved it.</i><br/><br/>Multiple instances hit me hard with their uncanny resemblance to the current state of the U.S.; it was all very interesting. There were most probably more in the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText18030338878489155994" style="display:none">Well done, Chainani, well done.<br /><br />A <i>significantly</i> more delightful book than the previous, and much less frustrating; my poor, tired heart is very thankful. It was more-so a rollercoaster that slowed down, picked up, slowed down, picked up, and kept switching that around until the end where it’s like forty loops in one go. <i>And I loved it.</i><br /><br />Multiple instances hit me hard with their uncanny resemblance to the current state of the U.S.; it was all very interesting. There were most probably more in the first book, but honestly I didn’t catch them... Maybe because I was too busy tearing out my hair... But never fear, as stated before, I did not go bald like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Lady of the Lake <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> for this lovely page-turner!<br /><br />Something else that struck me was that, overall, this book resounded as one being about love. Like, this series is packed full of people loving each other, but the importance of love shone especially in this one. If I were to consider <u>A Crystal of Time</u> a love story, which I absolutely do, it’s one of the best, having woven in the concept of love so seamlessly and perfectly.<br /><br />Before I begin my breakdown of how I feel about all the characters, I wanted to address my thoughts on what is probably the most significant reveal in this book... Although, that significance could be debated on, considering just how many twists and turns were stuffed into these pages.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I’m... pretty “bleh” on the reveal of the parents of Rhian and Japeth (quick side note: I <i>absolutely</i> believe that Japeth’s first name is “Rafal”, because in <u>The Ever Never Handbook</u>, it’s stated that Rafal’s brother was supposedly named “Rhian”, and Evelyn Sader was madly in love with Rafal... so...). I originally had a theory that Arthur had been duped with magic to sire the boys, but Evelyn Sader their mother? It just felt so “But why though?” to me. It’s like... We’ve been so done with this woman for <i>such</i> a long time, and her relevance to this series has been quite slim, so the impact of the reveal was... eh. I honestly barely remembered her, and had to refresh my memory with Wikipedia. So it just felt a tad too forced to me, like she was trying to be shoehorned in and be important again because she already wasn’t very impactful. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Okay. Character time.<br /><br />Girl power <i>dominated</i> this book, and I was <i>thriving</i>. Agatha and Sophie got their shit together and enacted plan after plan like nobody’s business. I was living for Agatha’s smarts, and honestly, Sophie’s too. In fact, I was <i>anticipating</i> her chapters in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Camelot, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> because they were always packed with the “Game of Thrones”-esque political drama that I adore. What a concept, I know! But, <i>but</i>, I’m still very hesitant to like Sophie... the <i>whole</i> Sophie. The Sophie I like is the one who schemes against wicked foes undoubtedly out of love for her friends. But when she’s with those friends, and the love is filtered through her bratty attitude, I just can’t stand it.<br /><br />Tedros continues to have the thickest head in the universe. Since when did he frustrate me more than Sophie? Lordy Christmas, his tripe about “I have to do everything by myself because I’m the king blah blah blah” was so infuriating, especially as he deflected the perfectly sound logic from those opposing this stupid-ass mentality. Do I still stand by #KingAgatha or what? King Agatha knows her limits and when to ask for a bit of help... <i>CONSISTENTLY.</i> So, he’s a moron, but I still don’t aggressively hate him, and if I <i>have</i> to root for any king... who isn’t Agatha... I choose Mr. Meat and Sports.<br /><br />The. Coven. Witches. Are. Absolute. Queens.<br /><br />Clarissa Dovey is one too. It’s been clear since book one: you do not <i>fuck</i> with this woman. She will rip you to shreds. And then she’ll turn around and open her arms to hug those she loves. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rest in peace, Professor, and never let go of your best friend. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The King Reaper reveal was absolutely iconic. Glad to finally know what was up with that little kitty, and his unyielding love for Agatha is the purest thing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Hort... is so gross... and delusional... and entitled... and obsessive... I really don’t like him. He even makes me a tad uncomfortable, which is kinda hard... Nicola, I’m still not your biggest fan either, you’re just okay, but please get yourself a better man... please... You don’t deserve his Sophie-obsessed nonsense... or just his regular nonsense.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[As for the two big villain boys... The Terrible Twins Two: Electric Boogaloo, as I kept calling them in my status updates... they were fine. They worked. There was nothing especially special or never-before-seen about them, but they had their compelling moments. Like... Rhian kinda having a bit of a point with his ideals, warped as they’d become, their complex family dynamic in general (especially during that <i>intense</i> final confrontation)... aaaaaaand... Japeth-being-super-duper-in-love-with-Aric-like-hell-yes-loving-me-some-villians-who-hate-everything-but-not-each-other.<br /><br />But yeah. They were fine. *shrug* <br /><br />Still, R.I.P. Rhian, whose death actually hurt because of the beginnings of a turnaround he was showing, as well as just how fun it was to watch Sophie “Cersei Lannister” his ass, and him whipping back like Tywin. (Sorry to all y’all who have no idea what I’m talking about. It’s another “Game of Thrones” thing, don’t worry about it.) So, rest in peace, you morally gray bastard, unless you’re brought back... somehow... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As a final note, I think it truly hit me in this book just how many times dudes go without shirts in this series. It’s clear that there’s something in the Endless Woods’ water supply that makes guys partially allergic to shirts. So, obviously, what I must do to celebrate the final book (ohpleasedearlordletthisseriesendaftersixbooks) when it comes out presumably next year, is to keep a tally of every time a guy is shirtless in the finale. Maybe I’ll even reread and make a total count for <i>all six</i>. <br /><br />Stay tuned.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[#SnaricEverAfter <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Bonus</b>
</u><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was, ahem, waiting for Japeth to be revealed as canonically/explicitly attracted to men so I could post this little number in my status updates... but since it didn’t happen (in this book, ehehehe), I’ll tag it onto here for now:<br /><br /><i>*to the tune of “Uptown Funk”*</i><br /><br />JA. PETH’S. INTO GUYS. JAPETH’S INTO GUYS. C’MON Y’ALL! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1747491939" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <u>Quests for Glory</u></a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2912882857" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <u>One True King</u></a><br /><br />•••••••••<br /><br /><b>PRE-READ EDIT 7/2/18:</b><br /><br />Just read the preview, very, <i>very</i> late, I’m sorry (If you’d like to read it too, it’s <a href="http://ew.com/books/2018/05/25/school-for-good-and-evil-book-5-preview/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.)<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I’m like, Agatha, I love you darling, but you <i>gotta</i> think on your feet. <i>I</i>, a <i>dummy</i>, figured out that Rhian and the Snake were the same person, like, <i>ages</i> ago. C’mon, girl! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />•••••••••<br /><br /><b>PRE-READ EDIT 5/26/18:</b><br /><br />Cool cover, still suspicious if what’s inside will be as cool.<br /><br />•••••••••<br /><br /><b>PRE-READ EDIT 4/7/18:</b><br /><br />Wait. Hold up.<br /><br />A March 2019 release date!? <i>
  <b>MARCH 2019!?</b>
</i><br /><br />*faints*<br /><br />•••••••••<br /><br /><b>PRE-READ EDIT 4/6/18:</b><br /><br /><u>A Crystal of Time</u>... please, please, <i>please</i> don’t be a <i>waste</i> of time...<br /><br />Despite my hesitance, however, I am excited for my dearest Agatha potentially wrecking some shit and saving her friends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18030338878489155994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3605564713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3605564713" />
    <a title="Layla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109681904-layla"><img alt="Layla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602279778p2/109681904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3605564713?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Layla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Layla" href="/user/show/109681904-layla">Layla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062695178" href="/book/show/40139216-a-crystal-of-time">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/109681904-layla?shelf=re-read-2020">re-read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3605564713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12333891872277897899"><b>~3.25 stars~</b><br/>(Dropped 1.75 stars from previous rating)<br/><br/><u>
  <b>Re-read (10/27/20)</b>
</u><br/><br/> I honestly didn't think I would be rating this book so low, but I've feel like I've been reading this book for 10 years. I of course enjoyed it, but it felt a bit lackluster from what I expected. <br/><br/><i> here are my reviews for the previous books in the series:</i><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3404720445' rel='nofollow noopener'>The School for Good and Evil: ★★★★ .5</a><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/3178099642/comments' rel='nofollow noopener'>A World Without Princes: ★★★★</a><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3178099834' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Last Ever After: ★★★★</a><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3545270277' rel='nofollow noopener'>Quest for Glory:★★★★</a><br/><br/><br/><i>
  <b>what I liked:</b>
</i><br/>• I liked Sophie's character in this book.</span>
  <span id="freeText12333891872277897899" style="display:none"><b>~3.25 stars~</b><br />(Dropped 1.75 stars from previous rating)<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Re-read (10/27/20)</b>
</u><br /><br /> I honestly didn't think I would be rating this book so low, but I've feel like I've been reading this book for 10 years. I of course enjoyed it, but it felt a bit lackluster from what I expected. <br /><br /><i> here are my reviews for the previous books in the series:</i><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3404720445" rel="nofollow noopener">The School for Good and Evil: ★★★★ .5</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/3178099642/comments" rel="nofollow noopener">A World Without Princes: ★★★★</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3178099834" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Ever After: ★★★★</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3545270277" rel="nofollow noopener">Quest for Glory:★★★★</a><br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>what I liked:</b>
</i><br />• I liked Sophie's character in this book. Yes sometimes she was dumb, but she was acually useful. She actually did something ( Tedros can't relate). She didn't spend the entire book screwing everything up or whining which is what she usually does. She acted thoughtfully and things were going so great until the end. Which says a lot coming from me, because I never actually like Sophie.<br /><br />• Lots of connections to the original trilogy and we get to know more about Japeth and Rhian's past. How they came to be , and how they were able to take power. The part that made the most sense about their part was that Japeth and Aric were best friends (maybe a little bit more than that 👀). Of course the two sociopaths that kill people for sport were once <i>friends</i>. <br /><br />• it prepared me for the next book. I feel the urge to immediately pick up the next book and breeze through it. I just want to know what happens next! It was an actual hopeful cliffhanger, and not the one that destroys you.<br /><br />• as much as I think that Tedros is a mindless troll who needs to acaully do something for once, his relationship with Agatha is kinda cute. When they reunited I genuinely got happy. <br /><br />• the whole thing with Reaper. I genuinely forgot that part from my first read, and when I tell you I wheezed...<br /><br /><i>
  <b>what I didn't like: </b>
</i><br />• this book was too long. And for how long it was we didn't get enough. It dragged. I had to push myself to read it even when I was enjoying it and that's never a good sign. In fact, I might mention, I would have preferred it if this series was a trilogy. I don't know if the last three books were quite necessarily, or really related to the original concept of "the school for good and evil". Again, not that I didn't enjoy it, because I did.<br /><br />• not enough Hester, Anadil, and Dot. Come on Soman, isn't it obvious by now that they are the best characters? So... Why not give us more awesome trio content.... Please.<br /><br />• For someone who is supposed to be really cunning and smart, Rhian was kinda acting dumb at times.<br /><br />• it switched from 3rd to 1st narrative for one chapter?! Why? It was confusing. I get what the point of it was, as it was supposed to help us get more perspective from Dovey, but I still don't like it.<br /><br /><br /><br />Overall, this is a solid book. I think there was a lot of lost potential and it wasn't my favorite, but I look forward to FINALLY reading the finale. I've been waiting for this. I'm kinda scared to find out how this ends, but also excited.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12333891872277897899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14462951366903927990">4.5 stars<br/><br/>Wow! This has been quite a ride! <br/><br/>I wasn't planning on buying this book anytime soon. I still have to read a ton of books, but one of my closest friends bought this book for me on my birthday and boy, oh boy, I tackled her in a hug.<br/><br/>Anyway, this book absolutely destroyed me. Then again, a whole bunch of other books have too. <i>What else is new?</i> <br/><br/>We continue to follow Agatha and Sophie in a chaotic ride that made me second-guess who was really good and who was really evil, who I could trust a</span>
  <span id="freeText14462951366903927990" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />Wow! This has been quite a ride! <br /><br />I wasn't planning on buying this book anytime soon. I still have to read a ton of books, but one of my closest friends bought this book for me on my birthday and boy, oh boy, I tackled her in a hug.<br /><br />Anyway, this book absolutely destroyed me. Then again, a whole bunch of other books have too. <i>What else is new?</i> <br /><br />We continue to follow Agatha and Sophie in a chaotic ride that made me second-guess who was really good and who was really evil, who I could trust and who I couldn't. By the end, it left me shaking and shivering with the thought that what I just read blew my mind.<br /><br />The character's relationships strengthen and weaken (but <b>mostly</b> strengthen). I found myself rooting for Sophie and Agatha as they try to overcome these huge obstacles that make them question everything they once knew. Sophie is trying to do what she can to defeat Rhian, even if it means sacrificing herself. Agatha tries to rescue Teddy boy and her friends from Rhian's grasp. <br /><br />And the shocking, and I mean <b>shocking</b>, truth we've been waiting for has been revealed. When that happened my heart stopped and my eyes widened so much I thought it would pop right out of my head. Soman Chainani was leading us one direction and when the characters finally discover the truth, I was as shocked as the characters.<br /><br />AND THEN ENDING!! By this time, I was convinced that my head was going to explode.<br /><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Saif" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Saif" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif">Sara Saif</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=i-like-you-a-lot">i-like-you-a-lot</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2780226497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15239552004879557884"><p>That was quite something. When you read the 'epic conclusion to the NY times best selling series' you generally expect it to be that, the <i>conclusion</i> (although, readers like myself must have begun to distrust this line and the promise within). And if the author decides to continue the story, it's very likely that the new books are not as good as the originals and they end up distorting your love for them</p><br/>This series has me conflicted. I'm annoyed at having to read a continuation of the story when </span>
  <span id="freeText15239552004879557884" style="display:none"><p>That was quite something. When you read the 'epic conclusion to the NY times best selling series' you generally expect it to be that, the <i>conclusion</i> (although, readers like myself must have begun to distrust this line and the promise within). And if the author decides to continue the story, it's very likely that the new books are not as good as the originals and they end up distorting your love for them</p><br />This series has me conflicted. I'm annoyed at having to read a continuation of the story when it ended okay. On the other hand, this new series is insanely good? And more complex, and twisted, and it didn't have the things that made me mad in the first trilogy? Like, I really, really enjoyed it but feel pissed at myself for that? Gah.<br /><p>I will say that <i>Camelot Years</i> deals with significantly less LOLs than the first three books. I forgave them for their faults and the incessant back and forth because I was too busy laughing. The new series is more mature, characters are developed and the plot is digging deeper into their pasts.</p><br />The focus of the plot veers in dozens of places at one time and I found that distracting. There were literally so many things crammed into the plot, they were hard to keep track of. There is a large set of characters so that could be a potential reason. All I know is, it was super frustrating. Then there is this technique of dangling answers in front of the reader and yanking them back just before they can grab them. I hate that technique. Soman Chainani's plot uses this technique like fuel. The smallest of details are tantalizingly to learn. I do not like being teased.<br /><p>Crossing my fingers that I don't forget all of this until the last book comes out.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="15239552004879557884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8859632905463366203"><i>Agatha and Tedros were the wrong heroes for this war.<br/>But Sophie?<br/>Evil was her blood.<br/>She was the hero to slay this dragon.</i><br/><br/>SGE is one of my most favorite MG series. I loved the first 3 books, books 1 and 3 specifically, but I hated the 4th book. It was like the character development of the main heroes went out of the window (Tedros and Sophie's mostly).<br/><br/>But this 5th book redeemed the series for me. And who's the one that saved the book? You guessed it. None other than SOPHIE!<br/><br/>Yes. Sophie. The Evil Wi</span>
  <span id="freeText8859632905463366203" style="display:none"><i>Agatha and Tedros were the wrong heroes for this war.<br>But Sophie?<br>Evil was her blood.<br>She was the hero to slay this dragon.</i><br><br>SGE is one of my most favorite MG series. I loved the first 3 books, books 1 and 3 specifically, but I hated the 4th book. It was like the character development of the main heroes went out of the window (Tedros and Sophie's mostly).<br><br>But this 5th book redeemed the series for me. And who's the one that saved the book? You guessed it. None other than SOPHIE!<br><br>Yes. Sophie. The Evil Witch of the Woods.<br><br>Though I love Agatha and Tedros, Sophie took the crown on this book. Literally. Well, not yet but almost. <br><br>I did not like Sophie on the first books. Why? Because she was a selfish bitch. Although Agatha had tried to prove the opposite, she always manages to do something for her own gain; not minding any of her supposed friends. But on the other hand, she tried and tried to do what is good but in the end she ultimately betrays her friends to do what is good for her. Her and her only.<br><br>But why do I like her in this book? Because I was waiting for the scenes wherein she betrays her friends again and again but there was none! Instead she's doing her best to help Agatha and Tedros; for Tedros to get his crown back even though she do not like him one bit. She's doing it for her friend, her one true love. And she's doing it for the best if the Woods. This is what I call character development.<br><br>Agatha and Tedros were like chicken without heads on this book but Sophie? She has an agenda of her own. An agenda to save the Woods in the clutches of Evil. Namely, Rhian and Japeth. <br><br>Speaking of this two, I hate them but I loathe Japeth more. They paraded as the Lion and the Snake of this book. Rhian, or the Lion, I can somehow relate to. It's like a twisted Thanos story. Ugghh. Good reasons but wrong ways to do it. But Japeth? He is a psycho. An evil Psycho. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[An evil psycho who killed his brother in order to bring back his another psycho friend from which his brother tried to protect him from. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>This book made me question a lot of things and I can't wait for the 6th one. Hopefully it will be published next year unlike this book in which I waited 2 years to read it.<br><br>But, I think I already know the ending of it. Because..<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552277710ra/27187191.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8859632905463366203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2999058696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2999058696" />
    <a title="Bethany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3660666-bethany"><img alt="Bethany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579576507p2/3660666.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2999058696?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bethany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bethany" href="/user/show/3660666-bethany">Bethany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3660666-bethany?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2999058696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12036702337771649999">I think this is one of the smartest series for young readers and the second trilogy really hits its stride in A Crystal of Time. It's emotionally compelling, funny, juicy, and has some big underlying themes that feel very relevant. The content definitely feels a little older than the first trilogy with some crossover appeal into younger YA. This book is really getting into the truth vs. lies, including some real life parallels to things like manipulative political leaders and fake news, but in a</span>
  <span id="freeText12036702337771649999" style="display:none">I think this is one of the smartest series for young readers and the second trilogy really hits its stride in A Crystal of Time. It's emotionally compelling, funny, juicy, and has some big underlying themes that feel very relevant. The content definitely feels a little older than the first trilogy with some crossover appeal into younger YA. This book is really getting into the truth vs. lies, including some real life parallels to things like manipulative political leaders and fake news, but in a fairy tale world. I continue to love the nuanced characters and relationships, with the deep friendship between Sophie and Agatha at the heart of everything. There are twists and turns, perilous moments, high stakes (especially for middle grade) but also humor and a lot of heart. I thoroughly enjoyed my time with this installment.<br /><br />As always, there is also tons of casual diversity and upending of expected gender roles. There are definitely things in this book that I would be hesitant to give to a 10 year old, hence the suggestion that this is a bit more mature, maybe more like 12-14? Also, do be aware of content warnings for cheating, death, previous loss of loved one, and a scene where someone uses dark magic to become non-consensually pregnant (note that there is no sex involved, but still...). </span>
  <a data-text-id="12036702337771649999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16554567882781724612">Edit June 2020: ended up changing my rating from a 5 star to a 4 star!<br/><br/><br/><br/>✨<br/>✨<br/>“Past is Present and Present is Past”<br/>✨<br/>✨<br/><br/>Y’all omg thIS BOOK AHHH!!!<br/><br/>This book was definitely my favourite one out of the series, Chainani reallyyyy outdid himself! I loved new characters we met, how we got to explore more from our already beloved characters, and also how we got to dive deeper into characters from the past...!<br/><br/>I really have nothing bad to say about this book.   <span id="freeText16554567882781724612" style="display:none">Edit June 2020: ended up changing my rating from a 5 star to a 4 star!<br /><br /><br /><br />✨<br />✨<br />“Past is Present and Present is Past”<br />✨<br />✨<br /><br />Y’all omg thIS BOOK AHHH!!!<br /><br />This book was definitely my favourite one out of the series, Chainani reallyyyy outdid himself! I loved new characters we met, how we got to explore more from our already beloved characters, and also how we got to dive deeper into characters from the past...!<br /><br />I really have nothing bad to say about this book. My major problems with the last book were fixed in this one, and I didn’t spot anything new I didn’t like. <br /><br />Something I’ve noticed is that there is always foreshadowing in the first chapter of these books, so as I was reading the first chapter, I was looking for potential foreshadowing, but I wasn’t sure if it was actually was there. No spoilers but!! The first chapter is actually intense omg, read it well!<br /><br />I also loved how the lines were blurred between who is good and who is evil, as sometimes it isn’t always black and white, especially if you change the perspective you’re looking at. SO GOOD!<br /><br />Overall, I believe this book to be a full 5/5✨, just due to everything. I loved the plot twists we see throughout the novel (and one in particular with a certain furry friend), and just all the development we see and everything! I would recommend you read it if you’ve read the rest of the series!</span>

<div id="review_2431561971" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2431561971" />
    <a title="delaney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6270594-delaney"><img alt="delaney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553837637p2/6270594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2431561971?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="delaney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="delaney" href="/user/show/6270594-delaney">delaney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6270594-delaney?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2431561971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3600427133182773217">Excuse me, Soman Chainani, 624 pages is not enough because now I have to wait who knows how long until the last book... THE LAST BOOK IN THE SERIES. <u>
  <b>THE LAST BOOK</b>
</u><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1554346911ra/27312407.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Honestly, Chainani can give me a 1000 page book on just Tagatha cuddling or Sophie changing bath mats into dresses and I WOULD STILL READ IT. Just reading this book, this series, these characters are my children and my family and I am going to be so sad to not continue reading their stories. I am hoping that it will be an Ever After</span>
  <span id="freeText3600427133182773217" style="display:none">Excuse me, Soman Chainani, 624 pages is not enough because now I have to wait who knows how long until the last book... THE LAST BOOK IN THE SERIES. <u>
  <b>THE LAST BOOK</b>
</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1554346911ra/27312407.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly, Chainani can give me a 1000 page book on just Tagatha cuddling or Sophie changing bath mats into dresses and I WOULD STILL READ IT. Just reading this book, this series, these characters are my children and my family and I am going to be so sad to not continue reading their stories. I am hoping that it will be an Ever After ending (I don't wish that for the Snake though, he can go die!) but I am going to cry and--oh, yup, not going to think about it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1554348343ra/27312456.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>A Crystal of Time</i> starts off running--literally! It picks off with Agatha on the run from Rhian after he takes over as king and imprisons all her friends. It goes from there with nonstop action and so much crap just thrown at these characters and the world!<br><br>I think at some points the humor was jarring and ruined the mood, but, other than that, this book was SUCH a delight! It felt like I was reunited (with old friends and world) and IT FEELS SO GOOD...except NOW I HAVE TO WAIT. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543277814ra/26652482.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just love all the little Tagatha moments, Sophie being a badass enigma, Hort is soft, Tedros gets jealous of SophieAgatha friendship/homance, taking baths to enter a crystal ball, SheriffRobin team-up, the Coven, Evelyn Sader still causing mayhem after death...oh yeah, the fuckery that is named Arthur and his relationships with women just can not be contained within his pants! <br><br>I think this book is more of a set-up to the last book but I still enjoyed it. I especially loved reading from Dovey's POV...that chapter really tore me up it was so beautiful, I loved it. This book in general was SO GOOD. (Look at that hella gorgeous cover I might add.) The only thing I hated was the fact that I didn't have more time in a day to read it and had to read chapters here and there!<br><br>Tedros levels-up, as in he's growing just as much as Sophie is! I feel that this arc really lets us see his growth in character, something we got to see in Agatha and something we continually see in Sophie. So it was so refreshing for him to admit and realize he is selfish and isn't fit to be king but realizing that, yes, that is his throne and he's supposed to be king. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1554349975ra/27312510.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, we get jealousTedros™ that I have been waiting for. I mean he's jealous of Sophie but still hilarious that he wants to be part of their sisterly bond. And besides, Agatha is just too Good for BOTH Sophie and Tedros! <br><br>Tedros: this is my princess Agatha and this is Sophie, Agatha's princess. (shoutout to Parks and Rec!)<br><br>Sophie is still so complex and slaying! She pretends and loves and stays loyal. But above all, she cares so much for Agatha and that is so great to see, none of that Sophie causing drama and more Sophie helping fight drama in that dramatic flair. <br><br>And my daughter Agatha using her animal abilities, saving her prince in distress, and looking killer in black. She's just perfect, what else can I say? We all know she deserves to be queen but how about king? King Agatha? <br><br><br>The spoils:<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>-REAPER IS KING. A cat is king of gnomeland! Go Reaper--also go Reaper thinking Tedros wasn't good enough for Agatha! We all know that! <br>-The first years are so adorable! This isn't really spoilery but I mean they are just adorable!--brings back that first year Agatha, Sophie, Tedros nostalgia!<br>-Japeth and Aric...more than friendship? Possibly adorable? <br>-Dovey dying and seeing Lesso again X( can you not? That is the best ship there is!<br>-The dresss that Sophie wears um wow, stunning! <br>-Tedros thinking about meat and sport<br>-Tedros putting a locket into his mouth to find the last ring<br>-Tedros being so in love with Agatha it's so cute it is giving me cavities<br>-Like literally, the first chapter in his POV he is thinking about how awesome Agatha is<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText7737213946230090162" style="display:none">i think, out of all the books i’ve read from soman, this one is my favorite. the first three, four were okay. but this one? i <i>actually</i> love. <br /><br />one of the things i loved most? the tagatha scenes, of course. throughout the first three books of the series, these two were always on different pages. but now? they’re a team. they don’t hide their feelings and love for each other. they can be real with each other. and i love that development. i love that. <br /><br />another thing i loved was how this book delved into the shades of gray between Good and Evil. because it’s true — everything isn’t black and white. and i loved how soman discusses that, especially with rhian, making us sympathize with him knowing he’s the enemy. <br /><br />but the most BIZARRE thing in this entire book? in this entire series? <br /><br />reaper. <br /><br />the king of gnomeland? for five whole years? i almost got whiplash from the amount of times i had to reread that. i was in hysterics. just check my reading progress. i was .... just .....         <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer598143290484130738">WOAH!! This one continues on a crazy adventure as Tedros and Agatha must fight to regain Camelot. So many new aspects are brought in. From a strange crystal ball, surrounded in mystery to learning a cat may be more that just a cat! And Sophia is, once again, questioned more than anyone. By all but me. Honestly I really felt she has grown and matured for this book in many ways. She has come into her own and I finally sort of like her. Although she can still grate on me too lol. Tedros continues t</span>
  <span id="freeText598143290484130738" style="display:none">WOAH!! This one continues on a crazy adventure as Tedros and Agatha must fight to regain Camelot. So many new aspects are brought in. From a strange crystal ball, surrounded in mystery to learning a cat may be more that just a cat! And Sophia is, once again, questioned more than anyone. By all but me. Honestly I really felt she has grown and matured for this book in many ways. She has come into her own and I finally sort of like her. Although she can still grate on me too lol. Tedros continues to drive me nuts. His attitude toward Sophia, his blind faith in is father and not listening to other possibilities of how to do things. My heart also broke a little in this one. There is some tragedy.<br />Once again, I did this via audiobook and cannot say enough good things about Polly Lee's narration! I didn't even want to sit and read a physical copy. I sought out the audiobook. I have only ever done that with re-reads in the past. So this is a first! <br />Great story, neat twists on the known tales. I can hardly wait for the conclusion!!</span>

UGGHHHHHHH I WANNA KNOW WHAT’S GONNA HAPPEN TO SOPHIE AND TEDROS AND AGATHA AND EVERYBODY NOW THAT ALL tHiS HAPPENED!!!!!</span>

<div id="review_2344257854" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2344257854" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10379180-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507236632p2/10379180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2344257854?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/10379180-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2344257854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9957682827169423844">The false king, Rhian, now sits on the throne of Camelot while Tedros sits in jail awaiting his execution. Sophie is being forced to marry Rhian and Agatha has escaped, heading toward the School for Good and Evil. She must rally the kids from both schools to help fight Rhian and the Snake and rescue Tedros.<br/><br/>There is a lot going on in this book, but it’s fairly easy to follow. As usual the chapters switch between different characters points of view, so the reader gets a feel for what’s going on ev</span>
  <span id="freeText9957682827169423844" style="display:none">The false king, Rhian, now sits on the throne of Camelot while Tedros sits in jail awaiting his execution. Sophie is being forced to marry Rhian and Agatha has escaped, heading toward the School for Good and Evil. She must rally the kids from both schools to help fight Rhian and the Snake and rescue Tedros.<br /><br />There is a lot going on in this book, but it’s fairly easy to follow. As usual the chapters switch between different characters points of view, so the reader gets a feel for what’s going on everywhere. I also like how the author will have something going on in one chapter and in the next chapter he lets the reader know how what just happened actually came to happen (did that make sense? ). <br />There are many twists and turns throughout the book. Some you see coming, many that you don’t. The author does a fabulous job creating a story that the reader is unable to figure out. As hard as I tried to figure out how Rhian was the One True King, I never imaged what the answer was. It was truly shocking. The reader also gets a better feel for Rhian and the Snake in this book. You learn about their past and how they came to be where they are.<br />My favorite part in the book is the minor character that no one ever thinks twice about gets a major upgrade. We meet new characters and lose some. The ending has a surprising revelation that leaves it one for the next book which I am very much looking forward to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9957682827169423844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oT2hirJnk+NM5thUUBpejHCskUzyR748JtF1oOSWZKyTI1f7j0Itc4mEHYus+57aeu/itGDBcVdDasdHbNaD5Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sa+JQ6JPR5ydXkssi5iUgpMRDmzbMmGgZBuy0ONNnGODsX8yn2r5DFg8jvN3eVTUmVJ9lEm0rssBoAA3aw17Kg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17252336772321722743">Soman Chainani's first novel, THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List, has been translated into 26 languages across six continents, and will soon be a major motion picture from Universal Studios. <br/><br/>The sequels, A WORLD WITHOUT PRINCES and THE LAST EVER AFTER, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List as well. Together, the books of the series have been on the </span>
  <span id="freeText17252336772321722743" style="display:none">Soman Chainani's first novel, THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List, has been translated into 26 languages across six continents, and will soon be a major motion picture from Universal Studios. <br /><br />The sequels, A WORLD WITHOUT PRINCES and THE LAST EVER AFTER, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List as well. Together, the books of the series have been on the print and extended NYT lists for a total of 33 weeks.<br /><br />As a writer and film director, Soman's films have played at over 150 film festivals around the world, winning more than 30 jury and audience prizes, and his writing awards include honors from Big Bear Lake, New Draft, the CAPE Foundation, the Sun Valley Writer’s Fellowship, and the coveted Shasha Grant, awarded by a jury of international film executives. <br /><br />When he’s not telling stories or teaching in New York City, Soman is a die-hard tennis player who never lost a first-round match for ten years . . . until he started writing THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL. Now he loses all the time.<br /></span>
